=== page 131 ===
You stand ankle-deep in the rutted, filth-churned road
that cuts through the rotting heart of Nulb. Brigands
flank you — mail-clad thugs with hard eyes and cheap
blades, their tabards black as their hearts. Villagers
have scattered, shutters slammed, dogs gone silent.
A man pushes through the guards. Measured. Heavy.
Intentional. tall, weather-bitten, and scarred from
cheekbone to jaw. His chainmail is clean. His blade
gleams. His stare could freeze rot. A masterwork
longsword rests easy in his hand.
Voice gravel-smooth, “So, you’re the ones stirring the
muck. I get called off my post at the Manor because a
few strangers think the law in Nulb bends like
rivergrass?” He steps forward, close enough you can
smell the oil on his blade.
“I don’t answer questions from vagrants. I ask them.
And you’d better start talking before I start cutting. You
were told to stop. You didn’t. You were told to stand
down. You didn’t.”
He levels the longsword at your chest. “So I ask just
once, and only once: Who sent you? What’s your
business in Nulb? And do you think your blood is worth
spilling in the dirt of this gods-forsaken pit?”

=== page 133 ===
The wooden doors of the manor groan open and the
stench of sweat, steel, and old blood drifts into the hall
like a curse that never left. Heavy bootsteps follow —
deliberate, iron-shod, unhurried.
He blocks the doorway like a siege ram, his chain
shirt creaking as he crosses his arms. The spiked flail at
his belt rattles like a warning bell, and his gaze settles
on you with the warmth of a meat hook.
“You’re the ones sniffin’ round Valegrave, are ya?”
He lets the silence hang. “I am Gregor the Overseer,
didn’t know he was collectin’ pets. Lemme be plain.
Aldren don’t see just anyone. If you’ve come to waste his
time, I’ll carve that lesson into your ribs and send you
back down the river howlin’.”
His eyes narrow, yellowed with disdain. “Turn ‘round.
Crawl back to whatever pit spat you up. And thank
whatever gods you still beg to that I’m in a good mood.”
The Boatman’s Tavern smells like spilled ale,
riverweed, and desperation. A murmur runs through the
rough crowd as the doorway darkens.
A broad-shouldered half-orc pushes in, ducking under
the frame, built lean like a fighting mast but corded with
ropey strength. His skin is a mottled grey-green, sunbaked and river-hardened. A jagged scar cuts down one
cheek, and his left eye squints like he’s sizing up a mark
through fog and rain.
“Strangers in Nulb don’t drink here ‘less they’ve got
reason. And reason means mission. So let’s cut the hull
open and see what spills.”

Warden of the Drowned Keys
Keeper of the Boatman’s Basement for Lodriss and

Role & Presence
A narrow-shouldered man with a ropey strength, old
bite scars on his forearms, and a loop of iron links at his
belt. Hosk moves like a patient spider—soft-soled boots,
whistle kept between his teeth, eyes always counting
exits. He “keeps order” below the Boatman’s: receives
captives, breaks spirits, and schedules midnight
transfers through the hidden tunnel.
Personality
Bureaucratic sadist: Courteous voice, fussy about
ledgers and routines; cruelty delivered.

Listener, not talker: Files away every word.
Motivations & Goals
Keep the line moving: On time transfers through the
rear ramp and the collapsed-shack tunnel earn him
Lodriss’s coin and Selentis’s favor.
Protect the secret: The bar-trapdoor, hidden panel,
and kitchen hatch stay undiscovered.”

From behind a covered wagon steps Ivar “Two-Fingers”
Maddok—broad-chested, weathered, and grim-eyed. His
left hand, twisted and incomplete, grips the handle of a
rusted walking stick, while his right rests loosely near
the hilt of a shortsword hidden beneath his apron. He
sizes you up through narrowed eyes—less with
suspicion than with a merchant’s practiced desperation.
“You lot—aye, you’re new to the mud and stink of
Nulb, but I hear you ain’t fools. Listen close. One of
mine—wagon and driver—never made it past the grain
tower. Supposed to carry sealed goods straight to the
Temple’s back vault. Sealed. If it’s gone, if it’s opened,
I’m a dead man wrapped in temple parchment.”

=== page 138 ===
You’re barely through the fence when a lanky kid drops
from the hay loft, finger to his lips. He keeps his voice
low, eyes on the road.
“Good—it’s you. I’m Kiel. You want news on Selentis
and her lot? Listen close and don’t look up at the
house.”
“First thing: her brigands walk the road in pairs—one
talks, one watches. They swap at the mile post by the
split oak. If you shadow them, switch sides when they
do.”
“Second: signals. At the Boatman’s side door it’s two
short, one long—‘move now.’ At the ranch lane it’s long,
long—‘all clear.’ If you hear three short at night, that’s a
panic call and you should be elsewhere.”
“Third: cargo marks. Meat and hides for the Temple
carry a single red ring in chalk. Double ring means
armed escort and a runner ahead. Grey twine on a crate
means rush it straight through to the Boatman’s.”
He glances toward the ranch house, then back to you.
He slips you a scrap of twine, knotted twice.
“You didn’t hear this from me. If you help, I’ll put a
ribbon on the post when there’s more to tell—blue for
‘come now,’ green for ‘wait a night.’ Grey twine means
hurry. You’ll see it again.”
The stair tightens; lamplight and perfume roll down. A
mountain of a man plants a boot on the next step, one
hand on the rail, the other on a scarred cudgel.
Mardun: “Names first. I’m Mardun—folk add the
Brute when they forget their manners. This is Elvanna’s
Loft. We sell coin’s worth of comfort and quiet. We don’t
sell answers.”
(He tilts his head, weighing the party.)
Mardun: “Steel stays sheathed. Voices stay soft.
Problems stay downstairs. Break those rules and I carry
you back down one at a time. Clear?”
(If the party pushes past or keeps climbing, he shifts,
blocking the step.)
Mardun: “Ah-ah. You’re not here for silk and song—
you’ve got that hungry look. So—state your business.”

=== page 139 ===
Lodriss came to Nulb years ago as a camp follower,
attaching herself to various groups of soldiers, brigands,
and other mercenary types. Her skills as a survivor and
opportunist quickly became apparent, and she gained a
reputation for her charm, wit, and ruthlessness. When
the opportunity arose to take over the Boatman’s
Tavern and the adjacent market space, Lodriss saw her
chance to establish herself permanently in Nulb.
With her connections, she managed to gather enough
resources to buy the property, and through a mix of
bribery, charm, and intimidation, she made it into the
most frequented tavern and trading post in town. Today,
Lodriss is both feared and respected, using her position
to control much of Nulb’s illicit trade and gathering
information for her own gain.
Role in Nulb
Seen as the unofficial ruler of Nulb’s underworld, using
her influence to control the flow of information and
goods. Lodriss has a Dwelling on the westside of Nulb.

=== page 140 ===
Madame Selentis (a.k.a. Baroness)
Madame Selentis is not a queen of criminals or a selfstyled ruler of Nulb. She is something far more
dangerous—a loyal servant of Supreme Commander
Hedrack, sent to the lawless village to safeguard the
Temple of Elemental Evil’s covert operations. Once a
noblewoman of Verbobonc, she was marked for
execution after her father’s betrayal during the 569 CY
uprising. Hedrack ordered her extraction and placed
her under the watchful direction of Lucius Graeme. She
now serves as Hedrack’s political shadow in Nulb,
quietly stabilizing the village’s chaotic factions to protect
the Temple’s supply routes, recruitment channels, and
cult infiltration into the region.
“Madame Selentis” is just noble enough to command
respect in dockside dealings, and just obscure enough to
escape scrutiny by more zealous cultists. Her mask is a
masterpiece of survival, forged in the flame of disgrace.
Signature Spells & Use Cases
1. Charm Person (1st Level) Tavern Leverage: Cast
discreetly during conversations with smugglers or
captains (e.g., Ravan Vell or Tolub’s crew)
2. Suggestion (2nd Level) Spy Recruitment: Subtly turn
a rival’s informant to her side “I think it’s in your best
interest to speak to me first.”
From Noble Exile to Temple Agent
Family Disgrace: In 569 CY, Lord Eldris Krivaltis
was exposed for providing intelligence and aid to the
Temple of Elemental Evil. The family was stripped of
land and title.
Lucius Graeme’s Intervention: Acting on Hedrack’s
orders, Lucius rescued the young noblewoman from
prosecution. She vanished from public records and
reappeared in Nulb ten years later under Temple
protection.
Purpose Reforged: Nysera no longer seeks
restoration or noble status. Her role now is to serve
the will of the Elder Elemental Eye and Hedrack’s
command, ensuring Nulb remains a critical node in
the Temple’s resurgence.
Occupation of the Ruined Manor
Following the Temple’s defeat at The Battle of Emridy
Meadows , Nulb was purged by the allied forces of
Verbobonc and Veluna. The village’s central structures
—including a small manor—were heavily damaged and
left to rot. Years later, the manor was quietly reoccupied
by a small band of cutthroat bandits dispatched by
Smigmal Redhand.
“Such a lovely evening. Surely we can come to a… friendly
agreement.” - Madame Selentis

=== page 141 ===
Her Role Under Hedrack
Lady Nysera as Madame Selentis, serves as a strategic
field agent and political stabilizer, embedded within
Nulb by direct order of Supreme Commander Hedrack,
leader of the Greater Temple. She is not a cult leader,
priest, or military commander—she is Hedrack’s
“civilian” asset, meant to quietly:
Hedrack placed Nysera, as Madame Selentis in Nulb
to act as his proxy. She reports indirectly through
Lucius but acts in defense of his long-term plans.
Protect Temple leadership in the region
Coordinate logistics and smuggling without drawing
attention
Manage or undermine rival factions in Nulb
Monitor internal threats and relay intelligence to
Lucius and Hedrack
“She is a political shield and sword in velvet—where the
prophets make blood oaths, Madame Selentis makes trade
pacts and cuts throats behind closed doors”
Hedrack leverages Nysera as Madame Selentis in a
manner similar to how a general uses an embedded spy
master or diplomat behind enemy lines:
To counterbalance Belsornig and Romag, who each
control major cults (Water and Earth) with
competing ambitions
To serve as a liaison through Lucius Graeme, his
trusted courier and senior spymaster
To shield Temple operations in Nulb without
attracting divine scrutiny from Veluna or
Verbobonc’s nobility
To suppress rival factions or cultists, such as Skole,
Tolub, or Rentsch, when they threaten Temple unity
or supply lines
Her orders are clear:
Maintain deniable control of Nulb’s pirate,
smuggling, and slaving economy.
Monitor the Earth and Water cult agents and keep
their territorial ambitions checked.
Ensure all Temple supply movements into the upper
ruins or moathouse are unimpeded.
“I do not serve the Temple. I use it. As I do the Reapers, the
pirates, and any man who thinks himself above my gaze.”
Connections and Allies
Sir Torvel Hawkes
Loyal Knight and Commander of Selentis Men. A
grizzled, honorable warrior, Sir Torvel Hawke has
weathered decades of battle. His weathered face and
salt-and-pepper hair speak of experience, piercing gray
eyes burn with unwavering loyalty to Selentis. As
Selentis trusted seneschal and military commander,
Torvel protects her from the small band of Temple
enforcers and ensures her safety. His goal is to see
Nysera restored to her rightful place in the Viscounty.
Lakash Quallad
Nysera’s (Madame Selentis) relationship with her
younger brother, Lakash Quallad, is strained at best.
Lakash, now a devoted agent of the Temple, views
Nysera’s pursuit of redemption as foolish and
unattainable. While Nysera sees her brother’s actions as
a betrayal of their family’s honor, she cannot deny the
potential danger he poses. Their paths are destined to
cross again.
Role: Lakash acts as a liaison between Nysera and
the Temple. His ultimate aim is to see his sister rise
to power in Nulb while he strengthens the Temple’s
influence in the Viscounty.
Personality and Goals: Ruthlessly pragmatic, Lakash
views his sister’s ambitions as aligned with his own
but would not hesitate to betray her if she
jeopardized his standing with the Temple.
Boatman’s Tavern
Madame Selentis maintain a precarious relationship.
Skole: Viewed as an opportunist, Skole frustrates
the Selentis attempts to control trade. Selentis
Temple Brigands are regularly stationed near the
market to monitor his dealings.
Lodriss, Mistress of the Tavern: Aligned with Captain
Tolub, opposes Selentis ambitions.
Captain Tolub of the Iron Dagger
Selentis and Tolub, captain of The Iron Dagger
maintain a delicate balance of cooperation and
suspicion. Tolub operates as a powerful force on the
rivers, controlling smuggling, piracy and supporting the
Canon Belsornig.
Waterside Hostel of Nulb
Selentis has an uneasy relationship with the Waterside,
run by the sly and cautious Dick Rentsch. While the
hostel serves as a gathering place for cultists, pirates,
and mercenaries.
Roleplaying Tips for Spell Use
She never casts first. She lets others reveal aggression or weakness, then responds with cold elegance.
Every spell is part of a layered deception. A charmed NPC might be followed with a forged letter. A commanded
thug becomes bait.
Let players suspect she’s magical. Madame Selentis prefers plausible deniability. Most in Nulb don’t know she’s a
caster—only that her words carry unusual weight.

Maldrith is cold, analytical, and utterly devoid of
empathy. He is a fanatic, believing that death is merely a
doorway to true power. He sees all mortals as tools,
existing only to further Orcus’ domain. Unlike the hottempered Zelt, Maldrith rarely shows emotion,
preferring to manipulate from the shadows.
His ultimate ambition is not just to spread the
influence of the Crimson Reapers but to transform Nulb
into a necropolis, a city of the damned where the dead
serve and the living exist only to be culled. His rituals
carve dark ley lines into the town, steadily weakening
the boundary between the Material Plane and the
Abyss.
“Orcus does not ask for faith; he demands servitude.

of Orcus “To serve Orcus means to rule in the dead”

=== page 143 ===
Scene: Docks of Nulb — Twilight, as fog
rolls in from the river
The Crimson Trader rocks gently at anchor. The smell
of tar, brine, and something less wholesome wafts from
her hull. From the mist steps a tall half-elf in a dark
captain’s coat trimmed in crimson braid, silver chains
glinting at his chest. A rapier, elegant and coiled like a
viper, rides his hip.
He walks toward you with the gait of a man who owns
the dock beneath his boots. His dark eyes flick over your
gear, your posture—calculating.
[Marad pauses a short distance away, hands clasped
behind his back.]
“Ah. New faces in Nulb. And so few know the way
here by accident.” His voice is calm, rich, and polished,
each word deliberately chosen.
“I am Captain Marad Vesrek. I command The
Crimson Trader—and oversee certain… delicate
exchanges in this harbor.” A faint smile plays on his lips,
unreadable and practiced.
Marad Vesrek, Captain
Marad Vesrek, a calculating and ruthless pirate captain,
commands the slaver ship The Crimson Trader.
Operating under the guise of a simple merchant along
the waterways of Greyhawk, Vesrek is a key player in
the Temple of Elemental Evil’s covert operations. With
deep ties to the Slave Lords and rumored Scarlet
Brotherhood connections, Vesrek navigates a
treacherous web of alliances and rivalries to expand his
influence.
Personality
Vesrek is a manipulative opportunist, guided by an
unquenchable thirst for power. He operates with a cold
pragmatism, viewing every relationship and deal as a
means to an end. While capable of charm when needed,
Vesrek’s true nature is merciless, and he has little
patience for weakness or incompetence.
Manipulative, cunning, ruthless.
Charismatic when necessary, but primarily
intimidating.
Speaks with precision and authority.
Has no patience for weakness or sentimentality.
Frequently sharpens his weapons, even during
conversations, as a subtle intimidation tactic.
Quirks: Often uses Safeton slang, blending his rough
origins with his polished image as a pirate captain.
Background
Born in the slums of Safeton on The Wild Coast, Vesrek
rose from a life of destitution by sheer will and brutality.
His early years as a dockside enforcer taught him the
value of leveraging fear and alliances. A fateful
encounter aboard the Iron Tide, where he saved his
captain from mutiny, marked the beginning of his rise in
the ranks. After years of service, Vesrek commandeered
his first ship, the Crimson Reaper, which became his
ticket to wealth and infamy.
Early Life in Safeton
Marad Vesrek was born in the port city of Safeton, a
bastion of lawlessness along the Wild Coast. The son of
a dockworker and a washerwoman, Vesrek grew up in
squalor, learning early the value of wit and ruthlessness.
Spent his childhood in Safeton’s dangerous docks,
running errands for smugglers and thieves. Learned to
fight and survive in back-alley brawls. As a teenager,
Vesrek joined a smuggler’s crew, impressing them with
his quick thinking and ambition. During a botched deal,
Vesrek saved his captain’s life, earning his first
command aboard a captured sloop.
Piracy Beginnings
Moved from petty smuggling to full-scale piracy,
plundering trade routes along the Selintan River and
Wooly Bay. Gained notoriety for his cunning ambushes
and willingness to take high risks.

=== page 144 ===
Slaver Connection
Forged ties with the Slave Lords, offering them a steady
supply of captives from his raids. Established trade
routes from Narwell up the Selintan River to the Nyr
Dyv, then westward to Verbobonc.
The Crimson Trader
Captured the Crimson Trader, a sleek galley equipped
for both speed and brutality, during a daring raid.
Modified the ship for slaving operations, outfitting its
holds to transport captives in secrecy.
Motivations
Captain Vesrek is driven by power, wealth, and loyalty
to his devil patron. While he serves the Slave Lords and
the Temple of Elemental Evil, he harbors ambitions to
expand his influence further. The discovery of a
powerful artifact like the Yellowskull could become an
obsession if he learns of its existence. Vesrek’s
ambitions extend beyond Nulb and the Slave Lords. His
ultimate goal is to establish his own dominion.
“Do you know what I see when I look at you? A
gamble. let’s hope your odds are better than your
manners.” - Captain Marad - Slaver Pirate
Relationships
Gefreid Patris & Madame Selentis: Limited direct
contact but occasionally delivers slaves and
contraband indirectly through Nulb’s logistics.
Lorveth Thrask “The Broker”: Close but volatile
relationship; frequent negotiations for slaves.
The Slave Trade Nexus: Captain Vesrek maintains a
lucrative and secretive relationship with the ‘Broker’
at the Boatman’s Brothel. This partnership fueling
the slave trade.
Belsornig (Water Temple): Crucial partnership,
regularly providing slaves for rituals.
Tactics
Begins combat with Mage Armor or Shield.
Uses Booming Blade with rapier.
Misty Step for quick repositioning.
Minor Conjuration to create distractions, “hidden”
keys, or falsified manifests.
Counterspell disrupts enemy spellcasters; used
tactically when he expects interference.

You step into the aisle; she looks up from brushing a bay gelding, braid a little crooked, cheeks smudged with dust.
“Hi. I’m Mira. Watch your boots—fresh straw. You look… not like pirates. Good. We’ve had enough of those.”
“You here for board or for trouble? Because we’ve got both. Dad says it’s ‘just the way of Nulb,’ but you can smell the
fear in the hay.”
“So—our problems. You should know them if you’re sticking around. First, debts. My dad owes coin to men who
collect with cudgels. Every time I save up to leave, a new ‘fee’ shows up.”
“Second, thieves. Tack walks off. Nets, too. If you see a grey-twine seal on a crate, it’ll be gone by nightfall, and
someone will swear it was never here.”
“Third, wolves in coats—pirates, Reapers, Temple folk. They stable their mounts and pay late, or not at all. They
think the stalls come with silence. I don’t sell that.”
“You… you look like you help people. If you’re here to help, you can help quiet: bring word to the constable when you
see men moving at last bell, or stand by the gate when the loud ones try to ‘borrow’ our best saddle again. Maybe walk
me to the mill some mornings so I don’t get followed.”
“If you are the helpful kind, I need three things: a farrier’s rasp that isn’t dull, a quiet word with anyone who thinks
debts come with free stabling, and a promise you’ll keep trouble out of my barn. Do that, and I’ll tell you when the
crates roll and who tries not to be seen.”

“Mother says I’m the reason she’s so old. I say she’s the
reason I’m so mean.” - Murfles
Murfles, posing as Hruda Murfles—the sharp-tongued daughter of Mother Screng—is an undercover agent of Good
stationed in the seedy village of Nulb. Despite her rough, unappealing demeanor, Murfles is a highly capable
adventurer, bard, and an ally of Otis and Canoness Y’dey. Operating covertly to monitor the activities of the Temple of
Elemental Evil, Murfles serves as a key player in the fight against the spreading influence of darkness.
Personality
Murfles is sharp-tongued, pragmatic, and fiercely loyal to the cause of Good. Her “Hruda” persona is brash and
cantankerous, designed to deflect suspicion and mask her true role. Underneath, she is calculating and deeply
compassionate, though her years of covert work have made her somewhat cynical.
“If I had a coin for every idiot who thought they could outwit me, I’d own this village—and the next one.”
Background
Murfles hails from Furyondy and was trained as a bard specializing in espionage and subtle manipulation. Her bond
with Otis, Canoness Y’dey, and the broader coalition of Good grew through her adventuring career.

=== page 147 ===
Otis Fletcher
Otis is a rugged, stoic presence in the village of Nulb.
Known locally as a skilled smith and stable keeper, he
maintains a quiet yet undeniable influence over the
town. Otis appears to be nothing more than a seasoned
ex-mercenary running a simple smithy. His services are
essential to the rougher folk of Nulb, from fixing
horseshoes and crafting weaponry to maintaining armor
for those who require more than a blacksmith’s touch.
Early Life and Upbringing (534 CY - 540
CY)
Otis Fletcher was born in the small village of Hommlet,
a modest community in the Kron Hills under the
Viscounty of Verbobonc. His parents, hardworking
farmers, instilled in him the values of respect for the
land and community. Otis’s father, Zed Fletcher, served
as the local Militia Captain, a role that gave Otis early
exposure to the idea of service and protection.
Birth: 534 CY in Hommlet, Kron Hills, Verbobonc
Family: Son of Zed Fletcher, a Militia Captain, and
his wife, both respected figures in Hommlet
Early Influences: Exposure to his father’s role in the
militia; service and loyalty were instilled early
“The forge teaches patience. The sword teaches
consequence. I’ve learned both the hard way.”
Growing Affinity for the Wilderness
(540 CY - 551 CY)
Though expected to follow the family trade of farming,
young Otis was captivated by the wilderness. He
preferred the Gnarley Forest to the fields, spending
countless hours tracking animals and learning their
patterns. During one of his wanderings, he became lost,
only to be found by elves who lived deep in the forest.
These elves taught Otis skills in tracking, survival, and
respect for nature, sparking a life-long friendship with
them. His time with the elves led to his training as a
ranger, developing skills that would set him apart from
the average villager.
Friendship with Elves: Learned tracking, stealth, and
survival from elven mentors in the Gnarley Forest
Ranger Training: Formally trained by the elves,
advancing rapidly due to his keen aptitude and
affinity for the woods
Skills Developed: Tracking, archery, survival skills,
and a deep respect for nature and elven lore
Otis’s Animal Companions
These creatures use surprise and stealth to protect Otis
and assist in his vigilant watch over the Temple of
Elemental Evil’s resurgence.
Owls (2), Otis’s Faerie Companions: Sprites (4)

=== page 148 ===
Early Adventures and the Encounter
with Mordenkainen (551 CY - 560 CY)
Otis’s curiosity and skills led him on many adventures
across the Viscounty and beyond. In his travels, he
encountered a powerful mage named Mordenkainen,
who along with his apprentice, Bigby, aided Otis in
defeating a band of marauding trolls. This fateful
meeting left a strong impression on Otis and opened the
door for him to join Mordenkainen’s secretive
organization, the Citadel of Eight, a group dedicated to
preserving balance in the Flanaess.
Meeting Mordenkainen: Assisted by Mordenkainen
and Bigby in a battle against trolls near Hommlet
Invitation to Citadel of Eight: Recruited by
Mordenkainen as a ranger; joined the ranks of
notable adventurers
Skills Honed: Experienced in team coordination and
learned to work with a diverse group of adventurers
Return to Vigilance (570 CY - 574 CY)
Shaken by the events at Emridy Meadows, Otis
returned to the Gnarley Forest and the lands around
Hommlet with renewed purpose. He vowed never to
leave his homeland vulnerable again. Otis took up his
old role with vigor, patrolling the fields of Emridy and
the paths of the Gnarley, tirelessly clearing the forest of
any remnants of the Temple’s influence. He faced down
bands of straggling cultists, hobgoblins, and other
sinister agents who had survived the battle and fled into
the wilderness. He drove them out, using his knowledge
of the land to become a relentless sentinel against
encroaching darkness.
As word of his efforts spread, the fields and forests
slowly returned to normal. Villagers felt safe once more,
and the prosperity of Hommlet increased as crops
flourished and trade resumed. Adventurers still passed
through, but Otis knew that their interest in the region
was fleeting. Unlike him, they would not remain once
the land was “safe” again. The villagers began to rely on
Otis as both a protector and a symbol of resilience. They
no longer whispered questions of his loyalty; instead,
they looked to him with pride.
Reclaiming the Gnarley: Otis dedicates himself to
rooting out all traces of Elemental Evil from his
beloved forest.
Guardian of Hommlet: Resumes his role as the
protector of Hommlet and the fields of Emridy.
Restored Prosperity: Villagers thrive under Otis’s
vigilance, and the region’s prosperity is renewed.
Lingering Regrets and the Weight of
Responsibility (574 CY - 576 CY)
Otis’s grief over Serten’s death and his own perceived
failures weighed heavily on him. Despite the passing
years, he could not forget his absence at Emridy
Meadows or the possibility that he might have saved
Serten. As he patrolled the roads and forest paths, he
could not escape the haunting memories of the battle he
had missed, nor the implications of what might have
happened had he and the Citadel of Eight united in that
moment. He often found himself standing before the
ruins of the Temple of Elemental Evil, staring at the
stones as if trying to divine some answer. Had he stayed
in Hommlet, could he have prevented the rise of the
temple altogether?
Enduring Guilt: Otis is haunted by thoughts of what
might have been present at Emridy Meadows.
Frequent Patrols: Driven by guilt and responsibility,
he redoubles his vigilance over the Gnarley and the
paths to Hommlet.
Solitary Defender: The village thrives under his
protection, but Otis feels alone in his mission,
knowing he must remain vigilant.
Living Incognito in Nulb (576 CY)
By 576 CY, Otis took his mission a step further,
establishing himself incognito in the rough-and-tumble
village of Nulb. Disguised as an ordinary blacksmith and
ex-mercenary, he carefully monitored the Temple of
Elemental Evil’s growing influence. With rumors of a
new threat emerging from within the temple’s
shadowed walls, Otis saw this as his chance to protect
his homeland more effectively, using the anonymity of
Nulb’s chaotic environment to gather intelligence. His
vigilance was no longer just an exercise in redemption,
but a strategy to uncover and prevent threats before
they reached Hommlet.
Otis has no illusions about the danger he faces in
Nulb. He keeps his true identity and skills concealed,
maintaining the facade of a simple craftsman while
watching the Temple’s activities closely. He knows that,
should the Temple of Elemental Evil rise again, he may
be the first line of defense—a duty he has willingly
accepted, for he knows he cannot fail his people a
second time.
Otis’s Family: The Fletchers of Hommlet
Otis’s roots run deep in Village of Hommlet, where his
family has lived for generations at the Fletcher
Farmstead, fostering a legacy of strength, integrity, and
duty to the village. His parents, Zed and Mara Fletcher,
are still respected figures in the village, though age has
slowed them.
Father, Zeb Fletcher: Militia Captain of Hommlet, a
respected figure despite his advanced age, and a
protector of the village’s people and traditions.
Mother, Mara Fletcher: A kind yet formidable
woman, known for her wisdom and humor,
maintaining a steady presence within the Fletcher
household.
Younger Brother, Elmo Fletcher: Young Elmo has
grown up since Otis’s departure, now a familiar face
at the local inn where he can often be found nursing
a jack of ale. The villagers say Elmo takes after his
brother in spirit, though he lacks Otis’s polished skill
as a ranger.

=== page 149 ===
Hidden Identity and Purpose
In reality, Otis is far more than he appears. He is a highranking ranger knight and secret agent of the Kingdom
of Furyondy, working under direct orders to monitor the
growing threat posed by the Temple of Elemental Evil.
Disguised as a common blacksmith, he gathers
intelligence and occasionally assists adventurers who
share his commitment to thwarting evil. Otis was once
stationed in Hommlet but moved to Nulb when the need
for his covert oversight became apparent. He maintains
regular communication with allies in Furyondy and
Veluna, including Murfles and the druid Y’dey.
True Identity: Level 10 Ranger Knight, an agent of
Furyondy and Veluna.
Mission: To secretly monitor the Temple of
Elemental Evil’s activities and protect the region.
Allies: Works with Y’dey, Murfles, and his loyal
followers, including owls and sprites, to keep a
vigilant watch over Nulb and its surroundings.
Current Situation Village of Nulb
Otis Fletcher, now living incognito as a blacksmith in
the Village of Nulb, maintains a delicate balance
between his cover identity and his role as a vigilant
agent of Good. Nulb is a hotbed of both Good and Evil
factions, a place where intentions are masked, alliances
shift like shadows, and every action is subject to
scrutiny. The Evil factions, consisting of cultists,
bandits, and spies loyal to the Temple of Elemental Evil,
are vigilant and connected, making it nearly impossible
for Otis and his allies to act without risking exposure.
Otis is highly aware that any misstep could reveal his
true identity and disrupt his mission.
Otis operates cautiously, avoiding open
confrontations and limiting his interactions with
unproven adventurers or unknown individuals. His
every action is calculated, and he rarely offers aid unless
absolutely necessary. Together with Canoness Y’dey
and the spy Murfles, Otis forms part of an underground
resistance dedicated to monitoring the Temple’s
growing influence. They only reveal themselves to those
they have vetted or those who prove their worth in the
struggle against the Temple’s forces. Otis remains
resolute, biding his time and assessing each
development with the keen instincts.
Otis’s Purpose and Resolve
Otis’s true objective in Nulb is clear: he is there to
monitor the resurgence of Evil in the Temple of
Elemental Evil and to be ready to strike if the
opportunity arises. Recent intelligence indicates a
disturbing increase in the Temple’s activities, with
rumors of cultists, mercenaries, and monstrous allies
gathering strength. The malevolent forces that plagued
Hommlet and the surrounding lands years ago are
stirring once more, and Otis can feel the weight of
destiny pressing upon him. He knows that the battle
against the Temple may reach a crescendo soon.
If he encounters adventurers capable of mounting a
serious assault on the Temple, Otis will join them,
recognizing the necessity of combined strength.
However, he will not do so lightly; he understands that
his life and his mission are precious tools in the larger
fight, and he will not jeopardize either for a reckless
foray. Otis believes that only a well-prepared, focused
strike has any hope of success against the Temple’s
defenses. He values preparation and strategy, and he
looks for those qualities in others before he commits.
Readiness for Battle: Otis stands ready to
accompany adventurers in a decisive attack on the
Temple if a genuine opportunity presents itself.
Selective Alliance: Otis will join only those who show
careful planning and sufficient strength to stand
against the Temple’s forces.
Commitment to the Cause: Otis is motivated by a
deep resolve to see the Temple dismantled, but he is
pragmatic and cautious in his approach.
The Brewing Evil and Future Plans
Otis senses a resurgence of the evil that once cast a
shadow over Hommlet and the Gnarley Forest. The
Temple of Elemental Evil’s influence grows daily, and
whispers of its returning power echo throughout Nulb.
Otis understands that he cannot fight this battle alone,
nor can he rely solely on his covert allies. With the
arrival of new adventurers, he sees the possibility of
turning the tide, provided they have the strength and
resolve to match the Temple’s dark ambitions. Otis
dreams of a unified strike, a coordinated assault that
will finally silence the darkness in the Temple’s walls.
If Otis’s intelligence reveals a critical vulnerability in
the Temple’s defenses, he will dispatch messages to his
allies. Burne, the mage in Hommlet, stands ready to
provide arcane support, supplying spells and magical
insights for adventurers aligned with Otis’s mission.
Furthermore, should Otis uncover the full extent of the
Temple’s power, he will alert Burne, who will then call
upon powerful allies from Veluna and Verbobonc. This
organized force would be capable of launching a largescale assault, a final death-stroke against the temple.
A Rising Threat: The Temple’s resurgence is
undeniable, with increasing numbers of cultists and
mercenaries gathering.
Strategic Alliances: Otis can rally allies such as
Burne and summon support from Veluna and
Verbobonc if a full-scale assault becomes necessary.
Hopes for a Unified Strike: Otis envisions a decisive
and coordinated assault to eradicate the Temple’s
dark influence once and for all.
“You’re not from here. Ain’t hard to see. You move
like folk who’ve seen trouble—and are lookin’ to stir up
more. This village… it’s a pot ready to boil over. Bandits
sniff coin. Cultists pass for merchants. And those who
run things? They don’t pray to gods you’d want knockin’
at your door. Now me, I’m just a smith. I’m watchin’.”

A serving wench, perhaps in her twenties, strides up to
you with hips that sway like a pirate’s knife—measured,

down her back, and a scar like a question mark peeks
from behind one ear. A tankard dangles loosely in one
hand. The other—calloused and stained—rests too
casually on her hip.
She squints at you through narrowed eyes, lips
pursed around a smile that never touches her face.
“Ain’t seen you lot before. Not locals, that’s clear.
Mercs? Pilgrims? Or fools wanderin’ too far from the
safe roads?”
She jerks her chin toward a crooked table near the
back wall—half-shadowed by a broken lantern.
“Sit. Drink. Or don’t. But answer me this: What’re you
doing in Nulb? Who do you know here—and who sent
you lookin’?”
“The living walk past my gates, pretending they do not
hear the whispers. The dead have more to say than any
of them.” - Osric Vell the Gravekeeper

=== page 152 ===
Rom Khavernus is Zelt’s right-hand enchanter, a
battle-mage with a sharp tongue and sharper mind. A
product of Dyvers’ New Gentry, he was born to privilege
but now thrives in the underworld, carving a name for
himself in the Circle of Shadows. While other wizards
bury themselves in dusty tomes, Rom embraces the
thrill of combat, the dance of diplomacy, and the allure
of power. His magical skills are formidable, but it’s his
charisma, wit, and ruthlessness.
Among the Crimson Reapers, the men whisper a
nickname behind his back—“Hollow Jack,” a mocking
yet fearful title that suggests his deals and promises are
as empty as his conscience.
“I may not be the strongest mage you’ll meet, but I guarantee
I’ll be the last one you cross.”
Personality & Motivations
Rom is charming, clever, and utterly self-assured. A
gifted conversationalist, he is equally at ease negotiating
a contract, seducing a noblewoman, or incinerating an
enemy with a fireball. While he enjoys the finer things in
life—wine, music, the company of intriguing people—he
has a pragmatic ruthlessness that makes him
dangerous. To him, loyalty is transactional, and survival
is about keeping the right people happy while staying
one step ahead of the blade.
Rom’s ultimate goal? Power. Influence. Freedom.
He’s tired of playing second fiddle to Dyvers’ elites. If
Zelt offers him a path to something greater, he’ll follow
—for now. But Rom is always watching, always
calculating. He respects Zelt, even admires him, but he
is not above replacing him should the time come.
Personality & Motivations
Rom is charming, clever, and utterly self-assured. A
gifted conversationalist, he is equally at ease negotiating
a contract, seducing a noble, or incinerating an enemy.
“Magic is not about wisdom. It’s about power. And
power is about knowing when to use it—and when to let
others think they have it.” - Hollow Jack

=== page 154 ===
Skole is a prominent figure in the village of Nulb ,
overseeing the rough-and-tumble Boatman’s Tavern.
His gruff, imposing exterior masks a web of complex
alliances and insecurities, making him a central, albeit
reluctant, player in Nulb’s underbelly. The following
sections delve into his appearance, background,
motivations, and entangled relationships with the likes
of Lodriss, Tolub, and the Greater Temple Selentis.
Ex-mercanary Background
A Life Shaped by Loss and Resentment Once a
riverman and smuggler, Skole ended up in Nulb looking
for stability—a rare commodity in his life. Years ago, he
purchased a house in the village, intending to settle
down with a barmaid from The Waterside Hostel.
However, his plans crumbled when she ran off with a
pirate, leaving him to live alone in a house that now
feels cold and empty.
With no other options, Skole found work at the
Boatman’s Tavern and quickly became its de facto
proprietor. Despite this, he doesn’t own the tavern; the
true owner is Lodriss, a cunning woman with
connections that extend into Nulb’s murky criminal
networks.
Occupation: Once a riverman and smuggler, now the
acting barman of the Boatman’s Tavern.
Residence: Lives in a modest, isolated house he
purchased in better times, often sleeps at the tavern.
Past Connections: His knowledge of smuggling
routes and river operations gives him a unique
insight into Nulb’s illicit trades.
The Lost Love: Skole’s dreams of marriage were
dashed when the barmaid he loved abandoned him,
leaving him with lingering bitterness and regret.
Motivations
Caught Between Fear and Loyalty Skole is a man torn
between self-preservation and a desire for stability.
Though he reluctantly assists in Nulb’s darker dealings,
he tries to maintain a low profile and avoid being drawn
too deeply into the dangerous games of the village’s
power players. This cautious approach is complicated
by his fear of Lodriss and her lover, Captain Tolub, who
dominate Nulb’s criminal enterprises. Additionally, Wat,
a local figure connected to Alrrem of the Fire Temple,
has been pressuring Skole to serve as an informant.
This proposition terrifies him, as he knows the
consequences if Lodriss or Tolub were to find out.
Self-Preservation: Skole values his life and would
rather keep his head down.
Loyalty to Lodriss: Despite his unease, Skole feels
bound to Lodriss and fears her retribution should he
betray her trust.
Avoiding the Fire Temple: Skole is wary of Wat’s
requests for information, fearing that any association
with the Fire Temple result in deadly consequences.
Reluctant Ally: Skole is unlikely to openly ally but
may be persuaded who offer security against Tolub
or Lodriss.
Tolub and the River Pirates
Fostering Connections with Nulb’s Most Notorious
Crew of The Iron Dagger, the leader of Nulb’s most
feared The River Pirates crew, often frequents the
Boatman’s Tavern. As the mistress of Tolub, Lodriss
maintains control over the tavern, which doubles as a
hub for smuggling and black-market trades. Tolub’s
crew regards the tavern as their unofficial headquarters.

=== page 156 ===
Captain Tolub “Ironwake”
Once a river mercenary, now a feared pirate lord, Tolub
commands the Iron Dagger, a sleek river vessel that
preys on merchant traffic along the Velverdyva. Known
as “Ironwake” after annihilating a rival crew, he
positions himself as a protector of trade—but in truth, he
is the very threat he claims to deter. Tolub is ruthless,
pragmatic, and deeply ambitious, driven by a desire for
control over all river commerce.
“A good drink and a dirty deal—two things I never say no to.”
Tolub’s rise came from uniting rival pirates through
brute strength and cunning. Now a high-ranking
member of the Cult of the Crushing Wave, he supports
the Temple of Elemental Evil by transporting slaves,
goods, and agents along the waterways. Though not a
true believer, he sees the cult as a means to expand his
influence in Nulb and beyond.
Motivations:
Primary: Dominate river trade through piracy and
extortion
Secondary: Expand power through alliances with the
elemental cults
Relationships
Lodriss (Lover & Ally): Manages Tolub’s affairs in
Nulb through the Boatman’s Tavern. Their
relationship is equal parts convenience and loyalty.
Madame Selentis: A wary ally; Tolub respects her
influence but monitors her closely. Their partnership
helps preserve Nulb’s autonomy.
Temple of Elemental Evil / Cult of the Crushing
Wave: Serves as a key enforcer and smuggler for
Belsornig. Supports cult operations when profitable.
Tolub turns toward the dock with a lazy wave of his hand, the leather of his coat creaking like old rigging as he speaks
—his voice low and worn like a river stone, dragging on each word with the weight of whiskey and salt. “There she is—
the Iron Dagger. Sixty-nine feet of stubborn timber and sharper teeth than most of the whores in Nulb. Flat-bottomed,
built for the shallows, fast enough to outrun justice, and mean enough to make her own.”
He glances sidelong at you, one brow arched like he’s measuring your worth by the silence you hold. “Carries spice,
salt, slaves, sermons—whatever buys us drink and keeps the oars wet. You see that sail? That’s no merchant’s mark.
That’s the wave that drowns kings. You step aboard her, you best know your footing. She don’t take kindly to
hesitation, and neither do I.“

=== page 157 ===
Knight Commander of House Krivaltis ·
Lawful Neutral (Human Fighter 7)
Sir Torvel Hawke is the stalwart commander of Lady
Nysera’s (Madame Selentis) forces in Nulb and the last
loyal knight of House Krivaltis. A survivor of the Battle
of Emridy Meadows, he is both seneschal and military
strategist at Mayor’s Manor, ensuring order within the
chaos of the village. Stern, dutiful, and unshakably loyal,
Torvel represents Nysera’s hopes of restoring her
family’s honor. Though his sense of duty is unwavering,
he is pragmatic—willing to dirty his hands to preserve
what remains of Krivaltis pride.
Torvel stands firmly by Nystera’s side. He is a
battlefield veteran, scarred by betrayal but tempered by
years of hard service. While he serves with absolute
loyalty, he quietly watches Nysera’s alliances with the
Temple and criminal factions, wary of how far she may
drift from their shared ideals.
Role in the Campaign:
Oversees Old Mayor’s Manor (Location 33)
Protector and Guardian of Lady Nysera
Diplomatic voice and enforcer of Nysera’s will
Cautious rival to Tolub, Rentsch, and Temple agents
Secret Past
Tainted by Betrayal: Torvel fought at Emridy
Meadows under Verbobonc’s banner, never knowing
his liege — Lord Krivaltis — had secretly supported
the Temple. When the Krivaltis name was disgraced,
his service under their banner stained his honor by
association. This shame still festers, leaving him
desperate to reclaim dignity through loyalty.
Haunted by the Temple: Though he despises the cult,
Torvel recognizes that Nysera’s survival depends on
its protection.
Living a Lie: In Verbobonc, he is presumed dead
alongside Nysera (Selentis). Should his identity be
revealed, he risks execution for treason or exile as a
dishonored knight.

=== page 159 ===
Brask, Kurn Challenge
The road ahead narrows, edged by knot-thick roots and
sun-grayed fence posts. The rattle of wagon wheels
fades beneath the sudden halt of hooves and the wet
creak of leather harnesses. Two figures step from
beside a lichen-covered waystone—chain shirts dull
under the canopy’s green gloom, maces slung low like
iron promises.
One—the squint-eyed bull of a man with a halfgnawed cigar—grunts through his teeth.
Brask speaks first, voice gravel-worn:
“Travelin’ this close to Nulb without a name, flag, or
writ? That’s bold. Bold gets noticed out here. You with
the Reapers? The river folk? One o’ them Temple
dogs?”
Kurn, leaner, darker-eyed, adjusts the crossbow
cradled in his arms like it’s a question you ain’t
answered yet.
“Lot o’ curious folk on the road lately. Some vanish,
some don’t. Some pay toll. Some bleed. You’d be wise
to talk fast before someone else comes askin’ less
politely.”

=== page 160 ===
Wat serves as the stalwart barkeeper at the Waterside
Hostel, a position that allows him to oversee the
comings and goings of various characters that frequent
this notorious establishment in Nulb . His unique blend
of vigilance and subtlety makes him an essential figure
in the tavern’s daily drama.
Key Role: Barkeeper and observer at the Waterside
Reputation: Sharp eyes and even sharper wits
Wat’s Background
Wat’s background is shrouded in the kind of mystery
typical of many who make their lives in Nulb. He arrived
at the Waterside Hostel several years ago with little to
his name but has since made himself indispensable.
Past: Rumored to have connections with various
criminal networks.
Experience: Years of surviving in Nulb’s harsh
environment have honed his skills in handling
difficult situations and people.
Motivation
Wat is driven by a complex mix of survival instincts and
the pursuit of profit. His position at the hostel allows
him to leverage both legitimate and illicit opportunities.
Survival: Primary motivation in the chaotic and
dangerous environment of Nulb.
Profit: Seeks to maximize his earnings through any
available means, lawful or otherwise.
Personality
Wat’s personality is as complex as his background. He
is cautious with information, resourceful in crises, and
incredibly secretive about his deeper plans and
alliances. Trusts few and always assesses angles for
advantage. Shares little, a mysterious persona.
Private Room
Wat has a shield + 1, elven boots, normal longsword
and shortsword, a pair of matched and balanced
throwing knives (daggers), a gold ring set with a fire
opal (2,000 gp) in the hem of an old cloak on a peg.
Political Relationships
His relationships within Nulb are tenuous and always
shifting, dictated by the changing dynamics of power
within the town. He maintains a functional relationship
with the temple agents, knowing the importance of
staying on their good side.
Lady Nysera: Keeps a watchful peace with her.
Pearl: Not just a lover but a partner in crime.
Dick Rentsch: Wat and Dick Rentsch both manage
the Waterside in Nulb, but their professional
partnership masks a complex and secretive rivalry.
Each is unaware of the other’s true allegiances.
There’s an underlying layer of suspicion.
Fire Temple Agent: Serves Allrem (Temple Fire).
“Every secret has its price; some cost more than others.”

78-79 Wat, Barman from Waterside Hostel
Visits to coordinate with Skole and monitor activities
80-81 Dick Rentsch, Waterside Owner
Rarely leaves his establishment but appears for important deals
82-85 Rhennee Traders (1d3)
Stop by to relax and exchange news
86-95 River Merchants (1d2) guards (1d4)
eek information and potential trade opportunitie
96-99 Mysterious Hooded Stranger
DM’s choice. Possibly Lucius the Courier, or a disguised cultist
100
Special Encounter (DM’s Choice)
Introduce unique events or characters as needed
“Nulb is the Viscounty’s frayed hem—river fog, rutted road, and a hundred quiet bargains. Merchants
whisper, knives decide, and the Temple’s shadow buys what law cannot reach.”

=== page 163 ===
Daggercap Mushroom
Blackcap Bliss (Illicit
Alchemical Narcotic)
Thick, dark-hued resin or smoky tincture, often mixed
with dreamfoil or burnt over coals to inhale.
Effects: Induces euphoric visions, numbness to pain,
and deep sedation; frequently abused for dreamlike
states of forgetting.
Side Effects: Long-term use causes mood instability,
tremors, and increasingly erratic behavior.
Origins: Extracted from daggercap mushrooms
harvested in the Fens of Tor and refined through
swamp alchemical techniques passed among The Pit
or traded via pirate routes.
Slaver Captain Verek trades with the the lizardfolk of
Torfen in the Fens of Tor.
Village of Nulb – Nighttime Encounter Table (d100)
Use 1d4+1 rolls per night to determine number of encounters. Avoid duplicates unless tension is intended.
Roll % Encounter
Description
01-02
Forest Rats (Kiel & Edric)
Scaling rooftops near the docks, eavesdropping on a cultist meeting.
03-04
Greater Temple Brigands (1d4)
Shaking down a merchant unloading crates near the market warehouse.
05-06
River Pirate Crew (1d3)
Carrying crates from a rowboat to the Boatman’s cellar. Drunk and loud.
07–08 Skole’s Thugs (2)
Dragging a bloodied man to the alleys behind the Boatman’s Tavern.
09–10 Cult Courier
Cloaked figure hurrying along the Low Road, clutching a leather satchel.
11–12 Forest Rats (Tomas Thorne
Sits alone near the chapel ruins carving a wooden toad, humming sadly.
13–14 Crimson Reapers Scout
Watching the Imeryd’s Run bridge, marking who enters town after dark.
15–16 Drenched Merchant
A traveler lost in the fog and looking for directions to the Waterside.
17–20 New Brigands (2)
Stumbling drunk, arguing over who they should sign up with.
21–22 Cultist Proselyte
Whispering heresies to beggars near a shrine. Offers strange coins.
23–24 Edric & Edris Veyne
Racing across thatched rooftops, giggling. Drop a pouch near the PCs.
25–26 Broken Blades (1d3)
Following a suspicious traveler into an alley—likely to rob them.
27–28 Velwyn “Blackfish”
Leaning on a barrel, quietly flipping a coin, eyeing the PCs.
29–32 Grud Squinteye
Smoking and grumbling outside the docks, looking for his men.
33–38 Dick Rentsch
Walking with a satchel toward the Chapel. Disguised in a grey cloak.
39–40 Drunken Fisherman (1d3)
Loud and stumbling, calls the PCs “Temple spies!” and demands a fight.
41–42 Cult Watcher
Silent, standing under an awning watching the PCs. Vanishes if approached.
43–44 Merchant’s Mule
Loose in the street, chewing rope, loaded with minor stolen goods.
45–46 Smigmal Redhand’s Scouts
Two lean bandits quietly tailing someone—possibly the PCs.
47–49 Mother Screng
Collecting herbs and mushrooms under moonlight. Hisses if followed.
50–56 Crimson Reapers (1d2)
Chalking thieves’ marks near the Waterside Hostel. May notice PCs.
57–58 Rhennee Boys (1d3)
Quietly loading crates into a hidden boat. Twitchy, well-armed.
59–62 Edric Thorne
Hiding in a tree above a road. May drop a whispered warning on the party.
63–66 Imeryd’s Mist
The river fog rolls in thick and fast. Visibility drops to 10 ft for 1d4 hours.
67–69 Crimson Reapers Recruiting
Offering coin to a mercenary—asking if he’ll slit throats for the Temple.
70–72 Pirate Duel
Two pirates circle each other in the square, knives drawn. Betting forms.
73–80 Hostile Dog Pack
Five mangy dogs harass everyone. One wears a torn pirate sash.
81–86 Captain Tolub
Staggering from the Boatman’s, roaring for Grud, sword in hand.
87–88 Merchant Caravan (arriving late)
Oxen and men covered in grime. They ask where to find safety.
89–90 Madame Selentis (Rare)
On foot, flanked by her Sir Torvel and her brigands. Headed to the old mayor mansion.
91–94 Forest Rats Chalk Signs
Strange symbols drawn near the alleyways. May lead to a hideout or warning.
95–99 Veyne Brothers
Arguing over whether to sabotage a bridge cart. They spot the PCs.
100
Special DM Encounter
Choose a major factional moment: a secret Temple raid, a Nysera betrayal.

=== page 165 ===
The 3orcs Village Campaign Sourcebook for
the Village of Nulb: Overview
The 3orcs Village Campaign Sourcebook for the Village of Nulb plunges your Greyhawk campaign into the fetid heart
of darkness—where power is for the taking, trust is a currency few can afford, and every muddy alley hides a blade.
This is not a heroic frontier. This is Nulb: a rotting, lawless river-village teetering between rebellion, cultic corruption,
and pirate warlords.
Located on the fringes of the Viscounty of Verbobonc and steeped in the long shadow of the Temple of Elemental
Evil, this 165+ page supplement transforms the once-underdeveloped village into a fully realized, dynamic sandbox.
Factions clash, secrets fester, and the fate of the region may well be decided not in Hommlet—but in the back rooms of
the Waterside Hostel.
System-Neutral Design with 5th Edition Stat Blocks
While written with 5e stat blocks, this sourcebook is edition-flexible and drenched in classic Greyhawk flavor. Rich
characterizations, detailed locations, and interconnected politics make Nulb a lethal, living setting for any campaign
built on danger and deception.
Expand Your Campaign with New Adventures
The Village of Ostverk module enhances your campaign, introducing a robust setting where every corner of the village
holds a story waiting to be told. This supplement invites Dungeon Masters to over 30 Key Locations: From Otis’s
secret ranger forge to the grim back rooms of the Brothel of Nulb and the traitorous pews of the Church of the Elder
Eye.
Dozens of Fully Realized NPCs: Including Madame Nysersa and her Greater Termple Brigands, Captain Tolub and
his river pirates, secret agents of the Earth and Water Temples, and covert spies of Veluna and St. Cuthbert.
Web of Power and Intrigue: Pirates, cultists, mercenaries, and noble exiles struggle for dominance in a brutal chess
game of knives.
Expansive Faction Conflict: The Crimson Reapers, the Broken Blades, House Velkori, the River Pirates, and the
resurgent elemental cults create an ever-shifting political battleground.
Temple of Elemental Evil Integration: Nulb is no longer just a waypoint—it’s a vital gear in the Temple’s
resurgence, and home to whispers of an even deeper secret buried beneath…
Fully Scripted Dialogue and Encounter Hooks: Designed to bring your NPCs alive at the table—no filler, just
immersive grit.
Adventure Awaits Those Who Dare
Will your players align with the Greater Temple iron-fisted order, or join the pirates who seek to drown Nulb? Will they
uncover the hidden hands of the Temple—or be devoured by them? Every corner of Nulb holds danger, every NPC a
potential threat or ally. This is low fantasy at its finest—where morality is murky, alliances are fleeting, and survival is
earned by wit, steel, and guile.
Welcome to Nulb.
You don’t conquer this place.
You survive it.
System-Neutral Design with 5th Edition
Stat Blocks
The supplement is written with Wizards of the Coast
5th edition Dungeons & Dragons stat blocks, but the
lore, descriptions, and dialogue are designed to be
system-neutral, ensuring its usefulness across multiple
editions or role-playing systems.
Enhance Your Greyhawk Campaign
The 3orcs DM Supplement for the Village of Nulb
weaves new and compelling adventures into the rich
tapestry of Greyhawk, offering Dungeon Masters and
players a chance to explore a frontier brimming with
danger, intrigue, and wonder. With its detailed worldbuilding and system-neutral design, this supplement is
an invaluable addition to any campaign.

=== page 166 ===
3orcs DM Quests
The 3orcs Campaign Sourcebook for the Village of
Nulb is an essential companion for Dungeon
Masters looking to expand their Greyhawk
campaigns with thrilling adventures and
immersive storytelling. Positioned at the
crossroads of the village of Nulb, near the Gnarley
Forest and Fens of Torr, Nulb serves as a vibrant
and dangerous frontier village teeming with
mystery, compelling NPCs, and dynamic lore.
System-Neutral Design with 5th Edition Stat
Blocks The supplement is written with Wizards of
the Coast 5th edition Dungeons & Dragons stat
blocks, but the lore, descriptions, and dialogue are
designed to be system-neutral, ensuring its
usefulness across multiple editions or role-playing
systems.
Designed to complement classic Greyhawk
adventures such as the T1-4: Temple of Elemental
Evil or stand alone as a unique hub for new
campaigns, this supplement adds unparalleled
depth to the region, presenting adventurers with
an array of quests, challenges, and opportunities
to make their mark on the world. Whether
defending the town from raiding Blackthorn Orcs,
exploring ancient ruins, or navigating the tense
politics of Verbobonc, the Gnarley Forest and elves
of Celene, Nulb brings the Viscounty of Verbobonc
to life like never before.
